<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e3b3b320-1264-4ee1-b5e3-22ee505f83c5'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer3377762629564196500">Bec (The Demonata #4), Darren Shan<br/>Bec is a book by Darren Shan in The Demonata series. It is the fourth book of the series released but it is first chronologically. The protagonist of the book is the central character Bec. It is set in Ireland around 1600 years ago. The last line of the book, "Screams in the dark," is also the first line of the book, as well as the tagline for the novel. Bec is the end of the first part of the Demonata books, where the three protagonists are introduced.<br/>تاریخ نخس</span>
  <span id="freeText3377762629564196500" style="display:none">Bec (The Demonata #4), Darren Shan<br />Bec is a book by Darren Shan in The Demonata series. It is the fourth book of the series released but it is first chronologically. The protagonist of the book is the central character Bec. It is set in Ireland around 1600 years ago. The last line of the book, "Screams in the dark," is also the first line of the book, as well as the tagline for the novel. Bec is the end of the first part of the Demonata books, where the three protagonists are introduced.<br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: ماه فوریه سال 2007 میلادی<br />عنوان: نبرد با شیاطین : کتاب چهار 4 : بک؛ نویسنده: دارن شان؛ مترجم: فرزانه کریمی؛ تهران، قدیانی - بنفشه، 1386؛ در 373 ص، شابک: 9645360439؛ چاپ سوم 1387؛ پهارم 1388؛ پنجم 1389؛ موضوع: داستانهای نوجوانان از نویسندگان انگلیسی - قرن 21 م<br />ماجراهای داستان کتاب «بک» در 1600 سال پیش، و در دوران باستان، و در ایرلند رخ میدهد، در آن زمان، هنوز بخش بزرگی از ساکنان این منطقه به مذاهب باستانی، و اسطوره های کهن خود پایبند بودند، و آیینهای الهی، از جمله مسیحیت، چندان گسترش چشمگیری در میان آنها نداشت. در کتابهای بعدی رابطه ها با شخصیتهای اصلی داستان آشکار میشود... چکیده: هر شب هیولاهای شیطانی به قبایل منطقه حمله میکنند، جان مردم را میگیرند و آرامش همه را برهم میزنند. بک، دخترک یتیم قبیله، با گروهی از جنگجویان همراه میشود تا به کمک قبیله ای دیگر بروند. اما آنها ندانسته سفری را آغاز میکنند که شاید تمام قبایل - یا تمام جهان را از هجوم هیولا ها نجات دهد. ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="3377762629564196500" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186332238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12276587811903353281"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380353434i/706785.gif' width='340' height='269' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Before I give the review let me just start by saying that Darren Shan is one of my all time favourite authors and I am not a huge fan of horror, his writing, characters and plot’s just captivate me and keep me reading. I recommend all of his books. But this has to be one of my favourites in the Demonata series.<br/><br/><b>Characters:</b> 9/10<br/>I loved all the characters. There were evil ones and good ones; you’d think it would be as simple as that, but no. In most books, it’s black and white. “That guys the evil </span>
  <span id="freeText12276587811903353281" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380353434i/706785.gif" width="340" height="269" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Before I give the review let me just start by saying that Darren Shan is one of my all time favourite authors and I am not a huge fan of horror, his writing, characters and plot’s just captivate me and keep me reading. I recommend all of his books. But this has to be one of my favourites in the Demonata series.<br><br><b>Characters:</b> 9/10<br>I loved all the characters. There were evil ones and good ones; you’d think it would be as simple as that, but no. In most books, it’s black and white. “That guys the evil one, yay, you go stab him you hero! Kill that evil it!” Not here, you know Lord Loss is an evil SOB, yet here we learn he was always an ass, but that’s not the thing, Lord Loss is the one constant in all the books so far. And what can I say; him and his army of demons are just cool. Onto the main characters such as the one telling the story, I love Bec. She is just so awesome. She has to be one of the most badass heroines ever. Even though she is small and looked down upon she does not let others fight her battle. She goes in guns high ready to shoot down every demon out there. Yep, she’s not your average heroine, plus her super cool magic powers are also pretty wicked. Also, I liked the fact that her mind was not centred on the opposite sex or a boy; instead, it was centred around saving the world!<br>	<br><b>Writing:</b> 8/10<br>I am a terrible judge at peoples writing, so I’ll just say what I thought of it. It was good. Like most of his other writing, it kept me interested and reading. And I liked how he described what was happening to Bec, I felt as if I was actually there.<br>	<br><b>Plot:</b> 9.5/10<br>Ah the plot, I could go on forever talking about what happened in the book. SO, I decided to just sum it up into one sentence. It is 400 years ago demons are invading the world, a group of warriors (and Bec) must go on a journey to defeat them, and rid the world of the demons. Yeah, that sounds a little ridiculous. Read the goodreads blurb, it’s a lot truer and it makes a lot more sense. The plot is really good and keeps you interested, wanting to know what happens, every step of the way. The journey they go through is amazing.<br><br><b>Enjoy-ability:</b> 9/10<br>Very enjoyable, a fun read that will keep you enjoying it throughout the entire book.<br><br><b>Overall interestingness:</b> 10/10<br>What can I say? Overall, the book is really interesting. The plot is interesting, the characters are interesting, and it even has a tinge of romance. Isn’t that what makes a good book. Because it sure made a good book for me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380353434i/706786.png" width="325" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Only way to describe the book...</span>

<div id="review_431838690" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/431838690" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/431838690?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=magic-powers">magic-powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=part-of-series">part-of-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=monsters">monsters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer431838690" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10155737115235691286"><br/><b>“To be a druid is to embrace death, dance with it a while, and finally fall prey to it. That is why we'll never rule this world. We have the power to bend all men to our whim, but are forever pushing ourselves further,trying to fly higher...and falling” </b><br/><br/>Bec is a good book, different from the others, a prequel of sorts, very high in fantasy level. While the others were in more modern times and touched by our world, this one is instead high fantasy, in a desolate world not our own, one which follo</span>
  <span id="freeText10155737115235691286" style="display:none"><br /><b>“To be a druid is to embrace death, dance with it a while, and finally fall prey to it. That is why we'll never rule this world. We have the power to bend all men to our whim, but are forever pushing ourselves further,trying to fly higher...and falling” </b><br /><br />Bec is a good book, different from the others, a prequel of sorts, very high in fantasy level. While the others were in more modern times and touched by our world, this one is instead high fantasy, in a desolate world not our own, one which follows different rules for the demon world.<br /><br />It introduces the concept of chess in the book (kind of) or Lord Loss's beginning interest in it. Not sure how this story will tie in with the others later. It did occur to me I need to read these closer together, or else I'm going to start getting them confused. Each book so far is with different characters, order of events and time settings.<br /><br />I liked the main character for this one - a child priestess with good morals and a strong outlook in battle. Their world (can't guess what it is yet) was different than ours and the demons have free reign there. The young priestess was powerful and I thought may play an important role later in the series, but after that ending, I'm guessing the importance she plays will be more indirect than direct.<br /><br />As before there's a decent offering of violence and gore level for this age group, and Shan doesn't hold the punches back when it comes to displaying his creative mind and his knack for writing inventive fiction. How happy I am that this IS fiction. Don't think I could handle Lord Losses walking around...<br /><br />Not sure on the jab at Christians but guess it depends on their world and how it tied together. Understandable enough as a standalone but confusing with how it ties into the other stories. I'm sure as I keep reading, all will make sense and eventually be revealed. This will be fine to read as a standalone and then continue with others in the series, although I prefer and recommend starting from book one and continuing from there.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10155737115235691286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_613678747" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/613678747" />
    <a title="Ninth " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16228867-ninth"><img alt="Ninth " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406345299p2/16228867.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ninth " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ninth " href="/user/show/16228867-ninth">Ninth </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">Like gore? its yours.</span></div>

      NUMEY!

              <span id="reviewTextContainer613678747" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer869815317687947602"><b>
  <u>5 Celtic stars</u>
</b><br/><br/>Someone pushed the REWIND button!<br/><br/>Its fuckin 5th Century AD or so! Old times rock!<br/><br/>So stuff begins with a neat biology related thingy. Then we find that we have ANOTHER major protagonist.<br/><br/>BEC. Meaning "The little one", Chic with awesome powers. Magic, healing and stuff. And oh! <b>A BLOODY PERFECT MEMORY! </b>i.e She could remember everything she heard, saw, felt or remember every guy she dated and so on...Hell! Chemistry reactions would have been helluva lot easier if she gave that lil </span>
  <span id="freeText869815317687947602" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>5 Celtic stars</u>
</b><br /><br />Someone pushed the REWIND button!<br /><br />Its fuckin 5th Century AD or so! Old times rock!<br /><br />So stuff begins with a neat biology related thingy. Then we find that we have ANOTHER major protagonist.<br /><br />BEC. Meaning "The little one", Chic with awesome powers. Magic, healing and stuff. And oh! <b>A BLOODY PERFECT MEMORY! </b>i.e She could remember everything she heard, saw, felt or remember every guy she dated and so on...Hell! Chemistry reactions would have been helluva lot easier if she gave that lil brain to me.<br /><br />So this chic is in a rath, some kind of primitive fortress kinda structure. She is an orphan. She is the village priestess. Just 14! And like all of them priestess' in those movies, she thinks that she'll lose her powers if she does THAT (yes, That). Hard when Fiachna the smith, her crush is around. There are other friends. Goll, a veteran one-eyed warrior. Ronnan and Locran, fierce twins and others.<br /><br />These people are always getting attacked by Formorii(humans who have turned into demons) every night. Vicious monsters who just love humans coz humans taste great. So one fine night they decide to have a party, and attack. <br /><br />The men fight, the women fight, the children fight. Casualities. A kid gets his throat ripped. His father goes in angrily and becomes Formarii's Dessert.<br />The formorii go away. Ordinary day.<br /><br />Then one day, outta nowhere, this kid comes in. He runs like Flash. But is as brainless as you(Xp). The people christen him 'Run Fast', since thats the only thing he says.<br /><br />The King of the tribe sends a group of warriors to follow the boy to wherever he wants them to go. Goll, Fiachna, Ronnan, Locran, Orna(a warrior chic), Connla(Fuckin bragger) aaand BECKY!<br /><br />So they move on. Following the insane kid. They run into trouble. But the kid seems AWESOME! He helps them out. You'd love to read how.<br /><br />They reach another rath. And find a druid there. Drust, the druid is more cold hearted than your freezer at its max. He wants their help though. A scene(abridged) <b><br /><br />Our guys: Soo...we got these damn Formorii attakin our arses every nite. Dey seem ta get stronga an smarta.<br /><br />Drust: Ya really think tha' its da same ol' Fomorii shit attackin ya? NO! Its nut da fomorii thi' time, its da MUTHAFOCKIN' DEMONATA!<br /><br />Our guys: Ya talkin shit! Wat da fuck is the demonada?<br /><br />Drust: majikal Kreechas from anotha Universe! They are Talla , Stronga an Sharpa!<br /><br />Our guys: YAY! We doomed!<br /><br />Drust: Nut if ya lot will come wid me an help me close da tunnel. *explains stuff about tunnels*<br /><br />Our guys: We game! Lets whup sum demonic arse!</b><br /><br />So.. The Naughty Nine set off. Drust teaches Bec new magic tricks (which does not include a hat and a rabbit). Spanking her if she does wrong (Bad Druid)<br /><br />One night. They meet LOVELY LORD LOSS (Oops... Lowly)<br /><b>YAY! *Cheers* Go! LORD LOSS!!! &lt;3 </b><br /><br />And they fight. Becky somehow gets(steals) Lord Loss' strength! (Gimme back my powers, Bitch!)<br /><br />Lord Loss moves away. Promising them agony, depression, pain, torment, fear...blah...blah...and death. And oh! Tommorow will be the first session.<br /><br />And the next day... Death.<br /><br />Will some make out in time to close the tunnel? Stop demons from crossing? With Lord loss not on their facebook friends list. Find out.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />Orna dies brutally (grossest till date). Bec finds stuff about her family- aarooo!. Locran dies. Drust reaches his destination. Lord Loss learns Chess. Lord Loss curses all of them. Fiachna dies. They reach the tunnel... Rest for yourself to read.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Plot: </b>Loved the way the scenes are captured. Lots of feed for imagination. Drastic twists. Betrayals. Revelations. Gross deaths. Everything Darren Shan is good at. The ending was... A bit saddening. But I Loved it. <br /><br /><b>Characters: </b><br />Bec: Loved the character. Who wouldn't love a hot 14 year old girl blasting demons into smithereens? but the narration seemed like third-person rather than first.<br /><br />Goll: One eyed Warrior. Nothing much about him, but he's wise and has an awesome spirit.<br /><br />Ronnan and Locran: Awesome twins, love the way they kill demons. They face demons like demons.<br /><br />Fiachna: Seems like a playboy at first, but then he proves himself as a warrior and a man with guts.<br /><br />Connla: F-u-c-k-e-r from the start to the end.<br /><br />Run Fast: ABSOLUTELY LOVED THAT GUY! I THINK IT'S GREAT TO BE MINDLESS!<br /><br />Drust: Cold. Hated him at first. But at the end, the feeling changed. He's the best guy.<br /><br />LORD LOSS: OMFG! My role model(JK) How brutally he killed that woman! Bad way but He still defines the TEEN HORROR genre. He IS the demon for the job. Artery and Vein are here too!<br /><br />----<br /><i>
  <b><br />Bec: So... Dusty. I wos wonderin if ya cud tell me haw we cud close tha damn tunnel.<br /><br />Drust: Becky, Just Keep calm and follow Drust.</b>
</i><br /><br />---<br /><br />Coolio!<br />Thats that!<br />Celtic goodbye!</span>

<div id="review_222032866" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/222032866" />
    <a title="❄️ Propertea Of Frostea ❄️ Bitter SnoBerry ❄" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6626436-propertea-of-frostea-bitter-snoberry"><img alt="❄️ Propertea Of Frostea ❄️ Bitter SnoBerry ❄" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1448206779p2/6626436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/222032866?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️ Propertea Of Frostea ❄️ Bitter SnoBerry ❄" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️ Propertea Of Frostea ❄️ Bitter SnoBerry ❄" href="/user/show/6626436-propertea-of-frostea-bitter-snoberry">❄️ Propertea Of Frostea ❄️ Bitter SnoBerry ❄</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007231393" href="/book/show/864798.Bec">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6626436-propertea-of-frostea-bitter-snoberry?shelf=didnt-want-to-read">didnt-want-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6626436-propertea-of-frostea-bitter-snoberry?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6626436-propertea-of-frostea-bitter-snoberry?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6626436-propertea-of-frostea-bitter-snoberry?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer222032866" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8478666144446294100"><b>Bec. The Little One. The one who Lord Loss has shared magic with... The book was so scary and had lots of gore! Bran was a good one :) <i>Run Fast!</i> :D What made me wonder was the theme of the book...Lord Loss didn't know chess then...the gods were Celtic and the year was 5th century AD....</b><br/><br/><br/><br/>Also, the most painful thing in the book...<br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[<br/><br/><b>Found it...</b><br/><br/><br/>I look around. Everyone’s awake. All eyes are focused on the spot from where the sound came. Ronan’s bow is aimed, an arrow ready to fly at its </span></span>
  <span id="freeText8478666144446294100" style="display:none"><b>Bec. The Little One. The one who Lord Loss has shared magic with... The book was so scary and had lots of gore! Bran was a good one :) <i>Run Fast!</i> :D What made me wonder was the theme of the book...Lord Loss didn't know chess then...the gods were Celtic and the year was 5th century AD....</b><br /><br /><br /><br />Also, the most painful thing in the book...<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br /><br /><b>Found it...</b><br /><br /><br />I look around. Everyone’s awake. All eyes are focused on the spot from where the sound came. Ronan’s bow is aimed, an arrow ready to fly at its target the moment he sights one. <br />“Don’t move,” Drust whispers, just loud enough for all to hear. “The spells are still intact. This might be nothing to do with—” <br /><br />“<i>Motherrrrrr…</i>” comes a cry, clearer this time. A girl’s voice. Full of pain and grief. <br />“<i>Help us… motherrrr…</i>” A different voice, this time a boy.<br />“<i>So cold… motherrrr…</i>” A third child, also a boy. He sounds younger than the other two. <br /><br />“What is that?” Lorcan asks, nervously tugging at his earrings. <br />“I’m not sure,” Drust answers. “Only demon masters can mimic human voices. And the undead don’t retain the power of speech. Perhaps Lord Loss is manipulating a lesser demon.” <br /><br />“<i>Motherrrr… hold ussssssss…</i>” The girl again. Her voice sends shivers down the back of my neck. I want to run to her and wrap my arms around her, even knowing she can’t be human. She sounds young, scared, lost. <br /><br />“I don’t like this,” Goll mutters, his eye darting left and right, trying to pick out figures in the darkness. <br />“They might be real children,” Fiachna says. “The demon could be using them to trap us.”<br />“No,” Orna says, and there’s a tremble to her voice. “They… I…” <br /><br />“<i>Motherrrr!</i>” the elder boy cries, as if in response to Orna’s voice. <br />Orna stands. “No!” Drust barks, but she ignores him and takes a step forward, hands clasped over her breasts, face torn between terror and delight. Something moves in the shadows. Three shapes advance. Drust curses, then creates a ball of fire and sends it floating down the hill, to illuminate the creatures. Three children are revealed, stumbling forward. Undead. Their bodies are in good condition, most of the limbs are attached, the flesh isn’t ripped to pieces, heads on necks. But they’re definitely not living children. They move sluggishly and one boy’s missing an eye, the other both its ears, the girl some fingers. <br /><br />“My children,” Orna croaks, and although I was cold with fear already, now I turn to ice.<br /><br />Orna takes a second step down the hill. “Orna!” Goll hisses. “Stop! They’re not your children! It’s a trick!” <br />“But they are,” Orna says. Tears are flowing down her cheeks, a warrior no longer, all woman now—all mother. <br />“It’s a glamour,” Drust says softly. “They’re probably the bodies of other children disguised to look like yours.” <br />“No,” Orna says. “I’d know my young loves anywhere.”<br /><br />“<i>Cold… motherrrr…</i>” the youngest boy moans. “<i>Lonely… motherrrr…</i>” the girl wails. Orna takes a third step. <br />“They’ll kill you,” Fiachna says. He gets up, breaking his masking spell. Moves towards her, hands outspread. “If you go to them, they’ll slaughter you, like the demons slaughtered them. It doesn’t matter if they were your children. They’re the Demonata’s now. They’re Lord Loss’s.” He shouts, scaring us all, “You’re out there, aren’t you, demon lord? Watching this and grinning, aye?” No answer, except more cries from the undead children. Fiachna closes on Orna and reaches for her, to lead her back to safety. Before his fingers touch her, she leaps away from him and draws a knife. <br />“Stay back!” she snarls. Fiachna blinks and lowers his hands. Orna looks at the smith pitifully. “They’re my children,” she whimpers. “I can’t leave them. They’re calling me.” <br />“<i>Motherrrr!</i>” all three wail at the same time.<br />“This is madness,” Goll says, stepping up beside Fiachna. <br />Orna points her knife at him. Goll glares at her with disgust—but with sympathy too. “Put your weapon away and come to us. You’ll see the folly of this in the morning.”<br /><br />“But they’re my—” <br /><br />“No!” Goll shouts. “They’re nothing except walking lumps of rotting flesh! Look at them, woman! Look with your eyes and brain, not your heart. Your children are dead. Accept that. Let this vision pass.” <br /><br />“But what if… maybe they could…” Orna’s shoulders slump. Tears fall more freely. Fiachna moves towards her again. Goll stops him and shakes his head— <i>wait</i>. <br />“Can we lift the spell?” I ask Drust. “Remove the glamour so she can see them as they really are?” <br />“No,” Drust says shortly. “She’s seeing with her heart now, not her eyes. No magic I know can combat a self-powered spell like that.”<br />“I could shoot one of them with an arrow,” Ronan says, squinting as he takes careful aim. <br />Orna growls like a wild animal. “You’ll die on that spot if you do!” <br />“Let her go,” Connla laughs cruelly. “If she’s so desperate to mother demons, who are we to stop her?” <br />“<i>Bricriu!</i>” Goll roars, the foul curse for a meddler. Connla only smiles. <br />“Please, Orna,” I mutter, trying another approach. “I need you. You’re like a mother to me. Let me be your daughter. I couldn’t bear it if you left.” <br />Orna’s eyes soften and she smiles. “You’re a good girl, Bec. And I love you, almost as much as I loved… love my little lost ones.” She shakes her head ever so slightly. “But you’re not mine. They are. And they’re calling me.” <br />“But—”<br />I get no further. In an instant, taking us all by surprise, she leaps away and is racing down the hill towards the three undead children, who raise their arms and croon with delight. Fiachna starts after her but Goll trips him. As he rises angrily, turning on Goll, the old warrior sticks his hands out, palms upwards, the sign for peace, then says softly, “Macha help her.” The fury fades from Fiachna and he turns to watch, along with the rest of us. <br />“You should have let me go,” he murmurs. “I might have caught her.” <br />“No,” Goll replies. “She was too far ahead and too desperate.” <br />Orna reaches the children and stops. I expect them to attack but they just stand there, staring at her, arms outstretched, waiting for her to hug them. For a moment I wonder if we were mistaken, if these are her children and mean her no harm. But then Drust nudges me and points to the right, further down the hill. I spot the outline of Lord Loss, inhuman eyes fixed on the woman and children, wicked smile visible even from here. Ronan fires an arrow at the demon master, then another, but both stop short of their target, as though they’ve struck an invisible wall. Lord Loss doesn’t even glance in our direction. <br />Orna kneels, extends her arms and draws the children in close. I see their faces, alight with evil glee. The eldest boy gently, lovingly brushes the soft flesh of her neck—then sinks his teeth into it. <br />Orna stiffens but doesn’t cry out. The girl latches on to the warrior’s upper arm, chewing at it like a dog with a bone. <br />The youngest boy’s head sinks beneath Orna’s shoulders. He rips her tunic open. I can’t see from here, but I know he’s suckling, drawing blood instead of milk. Orna’s arms tighten around the children, hugging them closer. <br />She hums a tune women sing to send their young to sleep. I gasp with horror when I hear that and turn away from the awful sight of the undead boys and girl feasting on the living flesh of their mother. Fiachna squats beside me and grabs me tight, letting me bury my face in his chest. “There there, Little One,” he coos. “She’s happy. She thinks she’s back with her children. We should all be lucky to die so willingly.” <br />“But they’re not!” I cry. “They’re not her—” <br />“I know,” he whispers, stroking the back of my head. “But she thinks they are. That’s all that matters.” <br />Although I’ve turned my back on the carnage, I can’t block out the sounds of ripping flesh and the occasional painful hiss from Orna or moan of satisfaction from the undead beasts. Even when I cover my ears with my hands, I hear them, or imagine I do. After a while the others turn away from the sickening sight, one by one, ashen-faced, eyes filled with regret, stomachs turning. Even cruel Connla, who gave up on her before anybody else.<br /><br />The only one who doesn’t turn away is Bran. The boy remains sitting where he awoke, watching silently, head tilted to one side, frowning curiously, as if he’s not entirely sure what’s happening and is waiting to see if this is a game with an unexpected, amusing finale. Eventually, since I can’t bear it, I walk over, turn him around and sit beside him. I lean against the simple boy and keep him faced away from Orna, allowing her the humble dignity of dying in private.<br /><br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Orna's death. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8478666144446294100" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2613919-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483904179p2/2613919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1213554251?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/2613919-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8176547-bec">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2613919-jason?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2613919-jason?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1213554251" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3866735440058044361">5 Stars <br/><br/>Bec, book 4 in the Demonata series by Darren Shan is a prequel to the series as a whole. What a remarkable rewind. Shan has struck gold with this one again and he did it with both an amazing plot and with incredible characters.<br/><br/>I loved little Bec(her name means "little one"). She is truly a fabulous main protagonist. She is likable and easy to empathize with. Bec is grounded, caring, and loyal. All attributes that are needed to be a successful priestess. Bec is not naive and is worldly. H</span>
  <span id="freeText3866735440058044361" style="display:none">5 Stars <br /><br />Bec, book 4 in the Demonata series by Darren Shan is a prequel to the series as a whole. What a remarkable rewind. Shan has struck gold with this one again and he did it with both an amazing plot and with incredible characters.<br /><br />I loved little Bec(her name means "little one"). She is truly a fabulous main protagonist. She is likable and easy to empathize with. Bec is grounded, caring, and loyal. All attributes that are needed to be a successful priestess. Bec is not naive and is worldly. Her character grows through out the story as do her priestess powers. She is awesome.<br /><br />Shan throws in quite a few bad guys into this story. Of course front and center is Lord Loss as this is the story that shapes the Demon Master's life and character. There are also several Humans that are nearly as despicable as him. Drust is one self centered and uncaring son of a bitch. There are other bad people but I won't give away any spoilers.<br /><br />What makes this book stand out?<br />1. Bec as our young heroine.<br />2. Drust for being a total asshole.<br />3. Bran "Run-fast".<br />4. Shan's magic.<br />5. The plot twists.<br />6. The very different feel to this prequel from the first three novels.<br />7. The violence and no punches pulled.<br />8. The amazing ending.<br /><br />Bec is second only to Kernel as far as I am concerned. She clearly wins in the powerful mage aspect but his voice and story will be tough to beat. This is a brutal book compared with the rest.<br /><br />I love this series and the Imagination and writing of Darren Shan. I am a huge fan. Bec is a remarkable prequel that works on many levels. I highly recommend this series to all that like urban fantasy that the older YA crowd would also enjoy.<br /><br />Fun!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3866735440058044361" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10161461670215590253">Bec <br/>By Darren Shan <br/>256 pages. United States. <br/>Little Brown & Co. $16.99 <br/>ISBN: 0316013897 <br/>(12 & up) <br/><br/>Are you ready to get mentally challenged? Not really, but this book will totally give you the worst nightmare. From Demons, to Druids then to human. This book takes place between 400 A.D and 500 A.D. –which explains why Christian was so unfamiliar to the people in the story. <br/><br/>Bec, the protagonist of the story is about to take on an amazing journey, a journey she would have never expected, and through</span>
  <span id="freeText10161461670215590253" style="display:none">Bec <br />By Darren Shan <br />256 pages. United States. <br />Little Brown &amp; Co. $16.99 <br />ISBN: 0316013897 <br />(12 &amp; up) <br /><br />Are you ready to get mentally challenged? Not really, but this book will totally give you the worst nightmare. From Demons, to Druids then to human. This book takes place between 400 A.D and 500 A.D. –which explains why Christian was so unfamiliar to the people in the story. <br /><br />Bec, the protagonist of the story is about to take on an amazing journey, a journey she would have never expected, and throughout this journey, she found out a part of her, a part of her that she was longing to discover for a long time. <br /><br />Throughout the journey, many themes will be shown, from friendship to betrayal, to leadership and more. Bec will have to make the biggest decision in her life. To risk her life and save the human kind? Or be a druid, being selfish? However, her ‘human-like’ heart, will lead her to the right choice. <br /><br />Along the way, Bec will meet a little guy name “Run-Fast”, why he stands out? No idea, I just like his name. But in the story, he has a special power distracting everything he wants to distract; his pure and innocent mind is not that bad afterall. But will this all help Bec during her mission? Is she going to turn her back on Run-Fast just to save the world, or whatever she wants to do? I guess you’ll have to read the book to find out. <br /><br />Not only the awesome theme attracts my attention, the awfully drawn cover just makes you want to keep looking at that book. However, you have to read the first 3 book to actually understand the book and really get into it. <br /><br />Darren Shan, did an amazingly wonderful job, preparing the readers (me) for the ultra surprising ending in this incredibly disturbing saga. He had gone above and beyond the fantasy world. Some of you might be disappointed, disgusted or whatever, but Darren sure did a good job making us hungry for the next book in the Demonata series. <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText6513444422185979068" style="display:none">My favorite book of the series so far. The ending was exciting and frustrating, and I felt so bad for Bec.         <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/29558240-bec">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2721522430&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2721522430" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7461462781796328736">Darren Shan has a habit of creating interesting and likeable characters and then killing them off as if they were no more important than a fly on a wall. On beginning the series, the constant and horrific bloodshed of innocent people, including young children and babies, can be quite overwhelming. However as you continue the series you learn not to grow attached to characters as they will more than likely be killed off at some point in the book.<br/><br/>Usually this does not include the main character, s</span>
  <span id="freeText7461462781796328736" style="display:none">Darren Shan has a habit of creating interesting and likeable characters and then killing them off as if they were no more important than a fly on a wall. On beginning the series, the constant and horrific bloodshed of innocent people, including young children and babies, can be quite overwhelming. However as you continue the series you learn not to grow attached to characters as they will more than likely be killed off at some point in the book.<br /><br />Usually this does not include the main character, so the ending of Bec surprised me greatly. It is because of this that I do not believe that we have seen the last of Bec. She was a strong-willed and determined character, which made her death all the more surprising. <br /><br />The jump between perspectives in each book confuses me as to which book takes place in which order, as he seems to introduce a new character in one book and then jump back to the main character from the first book in another. I have heard that the fifth book is going back to Grubbs Grady's (from the first book) perspective. I don't mind this as his story will not go unfinished, but I hope that he does not continue to introduce new perspectives every two books because I grow very attached to the characters and never hear about them again.<br /><br />I am mentally preparing myself for the next book in the series as the body count seems to get higher and higher as each book progresses. Something tells me that this won't change and the next book will be even more gruesome than the last.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7461462781796328736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_94855534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abby" href="/user/show/3461977-abby">Abby</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7032513710741280130">I've loved Darren Shan since I got hooked on his Cirque Du Freak series, and I didn't think he could top it. Guess what? I was wrong. BEC is the fourth book in the Demonata series, and it is probably the best series I have ever read. Ever. As far as BEC goes, I have to admit, it starts out pretty slow, with over half the book being Bec and her friends journeying to a new land. But after awhile it grabs you and doesn't let you go even after you've put it down - the ending will blow you away.<br/>Bec i</span>
  <span id="freeText7032513710741280130" style="display:none">I've loved Darren Shan since I got hooked on his Cirque Du Freak series, and I didn't think he could top it. Guess what? I was wrong. BEC is the fourth book in the Demonata series, and it is probably the best series I have ever read. Ever. As far as BEC goes, I have to admit, it starts out pretty slow, with over half the book being Bec and her friends journeying to a new land. But after awhile it grabs you and doesn't let you go even after you've put it down - the ending will blow you away.<br />Bec is an orphan of no known background studying to be a priestess in 400-500 AD. Her instructor is dead, she has no family, her powers are draining, and the only person that trusts her is Goll, a one-eyed retired warrior. Her people have been fighting the Fomorri, savage beasts later to be revealed as the Demonata. Then Run-Fast (or Bran) comes along. He's a simple-minded boy with a very limited vocabulary - but he manages to get Bec and some of her colleages to follow him to help another rath in distress. Or so they thought. The innocent boy leads them to a Druid named Drust, and after that Bec will learn her true place in life - but what will be the cost?<br />Bec is actually my favorite character in The Demonata, and is the first female protagonist Shan has ever had. Along with all the other books in the series, this one is really worth a read, but you'll need to read the first three, along with the six remaining. The tenth book in The Demonata, titled Hell's Heroes, comes out May 10th, and if I'm wrong, I know it's sometime in May.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7032513710741280130" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_543533116" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/543533116" />
    <a title="Paranormal_Madness" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17012067-paranormal-madness"><img alt="Paranormal_Madness" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468451974p2/17012067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/543533116?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paranormal_Madness" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paranormal_Madness" href="/user/show/17012067-paranormal-madness">Paranormal_Madness</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer543533116" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6029304268157916857"><b>What I liked:</b><br/>-Bec. I really love Bec. She’s a very intelligent girl, and she’s very resourceful. Not to mention she’s very selfless, especially in the end. I felt like she was very relatable, and it was surprising that Darren Shan could write such an authentic girl character as well as such authentic boy characters. I prefer Kernel, but Bec is probably my second favorite narrator.<br/>-Setting. I felt like Darren Shan did quite a bit of research about the world he was creating. It felt like I was rig</span>
  <span id="freeText6029304268157916857" style="display:none"><b>What I liked:</b><br />-Bec. I really love Bec. She’s a very intelligent girl, and she’s very resourceful. Not to mention she’s very selfless, especially in the end. I felt like she was very relatable, and it was surprising that Darren Shan could write such an authentic girl character as well as such authentic boy characters. I prefer Kernel, but Bec is probably my second favorite narrator.<br />-Setting. I felt like Darren Shan did quite a bit of research about the world he was creating. It felt like I was right there in her hut with Bec, and I could picture the gate and the walls of her home, and I loved how the magic was much more powerful back then than in the more modern books.<br />-The ending. It was perfect. As it was happening, all I could think was, “Holy shit, this is really happening! He’s gonna actually do it!” Then it happened just like I thought it would, and I was so amazed. It left me both angry and sad, and I wanted there to be just one more chapter, but there wasn’t.<br />-Gore. There’s plenty of it in this book, even though a majority of the book happens to be about the journey, not the fighting.<br /><br /><b>What I disliked</b><br />-Writing Style. There is a huge overuse of exclamation points, and it really drove me insane while I read this series, and some of the writing is very choppy, which can distract from the intense action and gore of the book.<br /><br />Overall, this was one of my favorite books in the series. I loved the characters and the magic and the setting, and I would definitely recommend this book to anyone that loves gore and fantasy and monsters. <b>5.0</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6029304268157916857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_92895712" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92895712" />
    <a title="Celine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3387843-celine"><img alt="Celine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460292659p2/3387843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92895712?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celine" href="/user/show/3387843-celine">Celine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007231393" href="/book/show/864798.Bec">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3387843-celine?shelf=demons">demons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92895712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11163908161689725135">While this book is often shelved as children's book, it comes with a warning: this series is Seriously Scary. And it definitely deserves this label. Darren Shan is a master in writing true horrifying stories.<br/><br/>Set in times where Christianity is rising and destroying the Old Fait, Bec doesn't know who her parents are. She is the sixteen-years-old priestess of a small town. When their town is being attacked by demons over and over again, she joins a small group of warriors sent off on a mission that</span>
  <span id="freeText11163908161689725135" style="display:none">While this book is often shelved as children's book, it comes with a warning: this series is Seriously Scary. And it definitely deserves this label. Darren Shan is a master in writing true horrifying stories.<br /><br />Set in times where Christianity is rising and destroying the Old Fait, Bec doesn't know who her parents are. She is the sixteen-years-old priestess of a small town. When their town is being attacked by demons over and over again, she joins a small group of warriors sent off on a mission that is destined to fail.<br /><br />The Demonata books are gory. There is a lot of detailed demon-slaying, and in Bec, also quite some casualties on the human side. <a href="http://nyxbookreviews.blogspot.com/2011/04/teaser-tuesday-24-bec.html" rel="nofollow noopener">An example of this you can find here.</a> This really isn't a fluffy tale to read to your child as bedtime story. Unless you want him to stay awake the whole night of course.<br /><br />Even for a violent book as this, the overall tone is very dark. Bec is on a mission that no one thinks will ever succeed. You start to feel for these people, their despair. Their home is raided again and again by demons, without any hope that they will stop coming. The tale of Bec's ancestors is so sad. Poor Bec.You can't help but feel sorry for the girl.<br /><br />Bec is not a book that will make you bounce happily through the house when you've finished it. But it's brilliantly written, and so, so gripping.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11163908161689725135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ms4b8YHIs2uultbnFk03O2Pwo4/R5ylqh8fbzAdhvZFHSzlFiE41YL2p0goZUYMohC5+OxMNunMm7vg9+KOajQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZZMc4yOQ2rEViULPz/284B/XUn8NtTo4gDg1TTNjhmO4Fj5XKhZcuga2RiLA4Qjz+AmPy89fqSEhERa8zKGhfw==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText10780831352335065409" style="display:none">Librarian's note: Also writes books for adults under the name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7790731.Darren_Dash" rel="nofollow noopener">Darren Dash</a>. Shan</a> and Darren O'Shaughnessy.<br /><br />Darren Shan (born July 2, 1972 in London, England) is the pen name of the Irish author Darren O'Shaughnessy, as well as the name of the protagonist of his book series The Saga of Darren Shan, also known as The Cirque Du Freak Series in the United States. He is the author of the series The Demonata, The Saga of Larten Crepsley, and Zom-B. He has also released the stand-alone novel, The Thin Executioner, and the stand-alone short novels, Koyasan, and Hagurosan. Plus, for adults, he released The City Trilogy (originally under the name of D.B. Shan), and Lady of the Shades.. </span>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/1052714-bec">Quotes from Bec</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Man wasn't made to share the universe with gods. Their ways are not meant for the humble likes of us. But we've decoded some of their secrets regardless. Like worms, we've grabbed on to the talons of eagles and learnt some small truths and means of flight. But we can never really fly. We try, and succeed to a certain extent, but the fall is always—will always be—there. To be a druid is to embrace death, dance with it a while and finally fall prey to it. That is why we'll never rule this world. We have the power to bend all men to our whim, but are forever pushing ourselves further, trying to fly higher… and falling.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/275426-man-wasn-t-made-to-share-the-universe-with-gods-their">30 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Bran,” I sob. “You have to go.” He just smiles. “Bran! You must!” Again the smile. He won't leave. He'll be my faithful friend forever. He'd rather die by my side than skip free without me. I return the smile. “Very well,” I sigh and reach out a hand. Bran takes it, expecting only my touch. But what he gets on top of that is the last of my magic. A swift, improvised spell. I reach into his mind and send an image into his thoughts, of the hole, him dashing out of it, racing through the cave and not coming back. And then, with all the magical force I can muster, I yell at him— “<i>Run fast!</i>&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/272990-bran-i-sob-you-have-to-go-he-just-smiles">29 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
